Subject: Earthwork Observation and Testing Report
Mass Grading and Site Work Development
The Villages of Kapolei
Village 8 Subdivision
Honouliuli, Ewa, Oahu, Hawaii
Grading Permit Nos.: GP2005-02-0104 and GP2005-12-0853
Reference: Report by PSC Consultants, LLC dated May 6, 2004
entitled "Geotechnical Exploration Report
Proposed Kapolei Village 8
Kapolei, Oahu, Hawaii”
Dear Ms. Sakamoto:
This report summarizes our geotechnical engineering services performed during
the mass grading, utility installation, and roadway construction for The Villages of Kapolei,
Village 8 Subdivision project development from March 16, 2005 through
December 12,2006 in general accordance with the Purchase Order Contract
(P.O. No. 3693-111) dated March 11, 2005.
PROJECT CONSIDERATIONS
The project site is within the existing Villages of Kapolei development in the District
of Ewa on the Island of Oahu, Hawaii. The project site is generally bounded by Kapolei
Parkway to the north, Kapolei Middle School to the east, Kapolei High School to the west,
and Kapolei Lower Channel to the south as shown on the Site Plan, Plate 1.
Based on the development plans, the proposed housing development has been
broken down into three phases, designated as Phase 1 through 3. As part of the overall
development, the project included site grading, house pad preparation; installation of new
utilities, such as sewer, water and drain lines; and construction of new roadways.
2006 Kalihi Street > Honolulu, Hawaii 96819
Phone: (808) 841-5064 + Facsimile: (808) 847-1749 »* E-mail: hawaii@geolabs.net
Hawaii ° California
Dick Pacific Construction Company, Ltd. Page 2
W.O. 5418-00 (Grading Permit Nos. GP2005-02-0104 and GP2005-12-0853)
March 8, 2007
This report addresses our field observations and compaction testing services
pertaining to the site grading operations, house pad preparation, and infrastructure
installation for the entire site. Observation and testing of the building foundation
excavations have been excluded from our scope of work under this report.
EARTHWORK OPERATION
As part of the Villages of Kapolei mass grading work, Oahu Construction
Company, Ltd. previously mass graded the project site. Dick Pacific Construction
Company, Ltd. performed the current site grading work and infrastructure installation.
The current site grading work generally involved fill embankments of up to 3 feet in
vertical height and cuts of up to 2 feet in depth to achieve the design finish grades for
the subdivision development. In general, the earthwork operation consisted of: clearance
of the existing ground, over-excavation of the surface expansive clays, preparation of slab
and pavement subgrades, placement and compaction of non-expansive select fill material
and base course, and utility tench excavation and backfill.
Following the clearing operation, the near-surface expansive clayey material within
the house pads were generally over-excavated (where necessary) to provide 3, 4, or 5 feet
of select granular fill (capping fill) in accordance with the recommendations presented in
the geotechnical exploration report prepared by PSC Consultants, LLC. Subsequent to the
removal of the expansive clay soils, the over-excavated subgrade was scarified to a depth
of about 6 inches, moisture-conditioned to at least 2 percent above the optimum moisture
content, and compacted to at least 90 percent of the maximum dry density as determined
in accordance with ASTM D 1557 (Modified Proctor). In some areas, the over-excavation
was terminated earlier if the near-surface expansive clay soils were removed and the
underlying in-situ coralline materials were exposed. In such cases, the top of the in-situ
coralline materials exposed during the over-excavation was proof-rolled to a firm and
unyielding condition prior to the placement of the select granular capping fill material.
The select granular capping fill generally consisted of imported coralline materials
generated from the mining operation at the borrow site to the southeast side of the
Kapolei Middle School. During placement of the select granular capping layer, the fill
materials were generally placed in near-level lifts not exceeding 8 inches in loose
thickness, brought to above the optimum moisture content, and compacted to a minimum
of 90 percent of the maximum dry density. The select granular fill material was capped
with 4 inches of topsoil compacted to a minimum of 90 percent of the maximum dry
density. The maximum dry density of the materials (referred to in this report) were
determined in accordance with ASTM D 1557.
A cavity was encountered at about the bottom elevation of SMH No. J6 during the
site grading operations. The cavity was exposed, cleaned of loose materials, and
backfilled with flowable fill. In addition, small cavities were exposed at the slope face of the
existing drainage channel during the preparation of Drain Outlet No. 4. The small cavities
GEOLABS, INC.
Hawaii ° California
Dick Pacific Construction Company, Ltd. Page 3
W.O. 5418-00 (Grading Permit Nos. GP2005-02-0104 and GP2005-12-0853)
March 8, 2007
were subsequently backfilled with concrete during the concreting of the drain outlet
structure.
The driveway apron and sidewalk slabs were also underlain by 3 to 5 feet of the
select granular fill material, as required by the project documents. Compaction
requirement of the finished subgrades of the driveway aprons were increased to a
minimum of 95 percent of the maximum dry density. During the course of roadway
construction, excavated coralline material generated from a nearby borrow source was
imported to the project site for the installation of the 3 to 5-foot thick coralline fill material
as stipulated in the pavement design sections for the project. Our office collected
representative bulk samples of the imported coralline materials from the borrow source
for laboratory testing to confirm that the imported coralline material meet the
requirement of a minimum CBR value of 25. The coralline fill material within the
pavement areas were generally placed in near-level lifts, brought to above the optimum
moisture content, and compacted to a minimum of 95 percent relative compaction.
New sewer, water, and drain lines as well as catch basins and manholes were
installed to serve the new residential development. In general, a bedding layer
consisting of 6 inches of No. 3B Fine gravel was provided below the piping and
manholes for uniform support. Free-draining granular materials consisting of No. 3B
Fine gravel was also used for the trench backfill up to about 12 inches above the pipes
to provide adequate support around the pipes and to reduce the compaction effort on
the initial trench backfill. The trench backfill was placed in 8-inch level loose lifts and
mechanically compacted to not less than 90 percent relative compaction. Where
trenches are below pavement areas, the upper 3 feet of the trench backfill below the
pavement grade was compacted to a minimum of 95 percent relative compaction. For
the sewer pipes, expansive clays encountered at the pipe invert elevations were
over-excavated to a depth of about 2 feet below the 6-inch granular bedding and
replaced with select granular material compacted to a minimum of 90 percent relative
compaction.
During the earthwork operation, samples of the on-site and imported materials
utilized as fill and backfill materials were obtained and transported to our office for testing.
The maximum dry densities and optimum moisture contents were established in our
laboratory in general accordance with ASTM D 1557 and the test results are summarized
on Plate 2 of this report.
Periodic field density tests were performed during the fill and backfill operations to
confirm our field observations as variations in construction procedures and soil conditions
were noted. A total of 3,508 field density tests, including retests of failed areas, were
performed using the Nuclear Probe Method in accordance with ASTM D 2922. The results
of the compaction tests performed are summarized on Plates 3.1 through 3.161 of this
report. These tests were taken on the prepared ground surfaces and on constructed
engineered fills and backfills at the site. Test locations and elevations were estimated by
GEOLABS, INC.
Hawaii ° California
Dick Pacific Construction Company, Ltd. Page 4
W.O. 5418-00 (Grading Permit Nos. GP2005-02-0104 and GP2005-12-0853)
March 8, 2007
pacing and interpolating from on-site survey stakes and construction plans. These
locations and elevations should be considered accurate only to the degree implied by the
methods used. Areas assessed to be unsatisfactory were reworked until the specified
minimum compaction was obtained and/or approved by our field representative based on
visual observation and hand probing.
Based on the observations of our field representative and the results of the
referenced tests, it is our opinion that the earthwork operations during the mass grading
and infrastructure installation for the above project observed and tested by Geolabs in
the period covered by this report were performed in substantial conformance with the
project plans and specifications and the recommendations contained in the referenced
geotechnical exploration report.
LIMITATIONS
It should be noted that it is not possible to continuously observe all activities
occurring simultaneously on a construction site. Therefore, some of the earthwork may
have been performed without our observation. However, the level of earthwork
observation and testing services provided appears to be reasonable in reducing some of
the geotechnical risks to the project. It should be recognized that there are variations in the
accuracy and statistical repeatability of the tests and methods used to monitor the
earthwork construction and materials. Our services were performed in accordance with
generally accepted standards of geotechnical engineering practice; no warranty is
expressed or implied. Provision of construction monitoring by an engineer is not insurance,
nor does it guarantee construction of any type. The contractor shall retain responsibility for
the quality of the work, for adhering to the plans and specifications, and for repairing
defects regardless of when they are found.
